initInstanceStore initializes the instance store based on the feature toggles.\n// It returns two vales: the instance store that should be used for writing alert instances,\n// and an alert instance reader that can be used to read alert instances on startup.\nfunc initInstanceStore(sqlStore db.DB, logger log.Logger, featureToggles featuremgmt.FeatureToggles) (state.InstanceStore, state.InstanceReader) {\n\tvar instanceStore state.InstanceStore\n\n\t// We init both stores here, but only one will be used based on the feature toggles.\n\t// Two stores are needed for the multi-instance reader to work correctly.\n\t// It's used to read the state of alerts on startup, and allows switching the feature\n\t// flags seamlessly without losing the state of alerts.\n\tprotoInstanceStore := store.ProtoInstanceDBStore{\n\t\tSQLStore:       sqlStore,\n\t\tLogger:         logger,\n\t\tFeatureToggles: featureToggles,\n\t}\n\tsimpleInstanceStore := store.InstanceDBStore{\n\t\tSQLStore: sqlStore,\n\t\tLogger:   logger,\n\t}\n\n\tif featureToggles.IsEnabledGlobally(featuremgmt.FlagAlertingSaveStateCompressed) {\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Using protobuf-based alert instance store\")\n\t\tinstanceStore = protoInstanceStore\n\t\t// If FlagAlertingSaveStateCompressed is enabled, ProtoInstanceDBStore is used,\n\t\t// which functions differently from InstanceDBStore. FlagAlertingSaveStatePeriodic is\n\t\t// not applicable to ProtoInstanceDBStore, so a warning is logged if it is set.\n\t\tif featureToggles.IsEnabledGlobally(featuremgmt.FlagAlertingSaveStatePeriodic) {\n\t\t\tlogger.Warn(\"alertingSaveStatePeriodic is not used when alertingSaveStateCompressed feature flag enabled\")\n\t\t}\n\t} else {\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Using simple database alert instance store\")\n\t\tinstanceStore = simpleInstanceStore\n\t}\n\n\treturn instanceStore, state.NewMultiInstanceReader(logger, protoInstanceStore, simpleInstanceStore)\n}\n\nfunc initStatePersister(uaCfg setting.UnifiedAlertingSettings, cfg state.ManagerCfg, featureToggles featuremgmt.FeatureToggles) state.StatePersister {\n\tlogger := log.New(\"ngalert.state.manager.persist\")\n\tvar statePersister state.StatePersister\n\n\tif featureToggles.IsEnabledGlobally(featuremgmt.FlagAlertingSaveStateCompressed) {\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Using rule state persister\")\n\t\tstatePersister = state.NewSyncRuleStatePersisiter(logger, cfg)\n\t} else if featureToggles.IsEnabledGlobally(featuremgmt.FlagAlertingSaveStatePeriodic) {\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Using periodic state persister\")\n\t\tticker := clock.New().Ticker(uaCfg.StatePeriodicSaveInterval)\n\t\tstatePersister = state.NewAsyncStatePersister(logger, ticker, cfg)\n\t} else {\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Using sync state persister\")\n\t\tstatePersister = state.NewSyncStatePersisiter(logger, cfg)\n\t}\n\n\treturn statePersister\n}\n\nfunc subscribeToFolderChanges(logger log.Logger, bus bus.Bus, dbStore api.RuleStore) {\n\t// if full path to the folder is changed, we update all alert rules in that folder to make sure that all peers (in HA mode) will update folder title and\n\t// clean up the current state\n\tbus.AddEventListener(func(ctx context.Context, evt *events.FolderFullPathUpdated) error {\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Got folder full path updated event. updating rules in the folders\", \"folderUIDs\", evt.UIDs)\n\t\tupdatedKeys, err := dbStore.IncreaseVersionForAllRulesInNamespaces(ctx, evt.OrgID, evt.UIDs)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tlogger.Error(\"Failed to update alert rules in the folders after their full paths were changed\", \"error\", err, \"folderUIDs\", evt.UIDs, \"orgID\", evt.OrgID)\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Updated version for alert rules\", \"keys\", updatedKeys)\n\t\treturn nil\n\t})\n}\n\n// Run starts the scheduler and Alertmanager.\nfunc (ng *AlertNG) Run(ctx context.Context) error {\n\tng.Log.Debug(\"Starting\", \"execute_alerts\", ng.Cfg.UnifiedAlerting.ExecuteAlerts)\n\n\tchildren, subCtx := errgroup.WithContext(ctx)\n\n\tchildren.Go(func() error {\n\t\treturn ng.MultiOrgAlertmanager.Run(subCtx)\n\t})\n\tchildren.Go(func() error {\n\t\treturn ng.AlertsRouter.Run(subCtx)\n\t})\n\n\tif ng.Cfg.UnifiedAlerting.ExecuteAlerts {\n\t\t// Only Warm() the state manager if we are actually executing alerts.\n\t\t// Doing so when we are not executing alerts is wasteful and could lead\n\t\t// to misleading rule status queries, as the status returned will be\n\t\t// always based on the state loaded from the database at startup, and\n\t\t// not the most recent evaluation state.\n\t\t//\n\t\t// Also note that this runs synchronously to ensure state is loaded\n\t\t// before rule evaluation begins, hence we use ctx and not subCtx.\n\t\t//\n\t\tng.stateManager.Warm(ctx, ng.store, ng.store, ng.StartupInstanceReader)\n\n\t\tchildren.Go(func() error {\n\t\t\treturn ng.schedule.Run(subCtx)\n\t\t})\n\t\tchildren.Go(func() error {\n\t\t\treturn ng.stateManager.Run(subCtx)\n\t\t})\n\t}\n\treturn children.Wait()\n}\n\n// IsDisabled returns true if the alerting service is disabled for this instance.\nfunc (ng *AlertNG) IsDisabled() bool {\n\tif ng.Cfg == nil {\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\n\treturn !ng.Cfg.UnifiedAlerting.IsEnabled()\n}\n\n// GetHooks returns a facility for replacing handlers for paths. The handler hook for a path\n// is invoked after all other middleware is invoked (authentication, instrumentation).\nfunc (ng *AlertNG) GetHooks() *api.Hooks {\n\treturn ng.Api.Hooks\n}\n\ntype Historian interface {\n\tapi.Historian\n\tstate.Historian\n}\n\nfunc configureHistorianBackend(\n\tctx context.Context,\n\tcfg setting.UnifiedAlertingStateHistorySettings,\n\tar annotations.Repository,\n\tds dashboards.DashboardService,\n\trs historian.RuleStore,\n\tmet *metrics.Historian,\n\tl log.Logger,\n\ttracer tracing.Tracer,\n\tac historian.AccessControl,\n\tdatasourceService datasources.DataSourceService,\n\thttpClientProvider httpclient.Provider,\n\tpluginContextProvider *plugincontext.Provider,\n\tclock clock.Clock,\n\tmw *metrics.RemoteWriter,\n) (Historian, error) {\n\tif !cfg.Enabled {\n\t\tmet.Info.WithLabelValues(\"noop\").Set(0)\n\t\treturn historian.NewNopHistorian(), nil\n\t}\n\n\tbackend, err := historian.ParseBackendType(cfg.Backend)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tmet.Info.WithLabelValues(backend.String()).Set(1)\n\tif backend == historian.BackendTypeMultiple {\n\t\tprimaryCfg := cfg\n\t\tprimaryCfg.Backend = cfg.MultiPrimary\n\t\tprimary, err := configureHistorianBackend(ctx, primaryCfg, ar, ds, rs, met, l, tracer, ac, datasourceService, httpClientProvider, pluginContextProvider, clock, mw)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"multi-backend target \\\"%s\\\" was misconfigured: %w\", cfg.MultiPrimary, err)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tvar secondaries []historian.Backend\n\t\tfor _, b := range cfg.MultiSecondaries {\n\t\t\tsecCfg := cfg\n\t\t\tsecCfg.Backend = b\n\t\t\tsec, err := configureHistorianBackend(ctx, secCfg, ar, ds, rs, met, l, tracer, ac, datasourceService, httpClientProvider, pluginContextProvider, clock, mw)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"multi-backend target \\\"%s\\\" was miconfigured: %w\", b, err)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tsecondaries = append(secondaries, sec)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tl.Info(\"State history is operating in multi-backend mode\", \"primary\", cfg.MultiPrimary, \"secondaries\", cfg.MultiSecondaries)\n\t\treturn historian.NewMultipleBackend(primary, secondaries...), nil\n\t}\n\tif backend == historian.BackendTypeAnnotations {\n\t\tstore := historian.NewAnnotationStore(ar, ds, met)\n\t\tlogCtx := log.WithContextualAttributes(ctx, []any{\"backend\", \"annotations\"})\n\t\tannotationBackendLogger := log.New(\"ngalert.state.historian\").FromContext(logCtx)\n\t\treturn historian.NewAnnotationBackend(annotationBackendLogger, store, rs, met, ac), nil\n\t}\n\tif backend == historian.BackendTypeLoki {\n\t\tlcfg, err := lokiconfig.NewLokiConfig(cfg.LokiSettings)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"invalid remote loki configuration: %w\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t\treq := lokiclient.NewRequester()\n\t\tlogCtx := log.WithContextualAttributes(ctx, []any{\"backend\", \"loki\"})\n\t\tlokiBackendLogger := log.New(\"ngalert.state.historian\").FromContext(logCtx)\n\t\tbackend := historian.NewRemoteLokiBackend(lokiBackendLogger, lcfg, req, met, tracer, rs, ac)\n\n\t\ttestConnCtx, cancelFunc := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 10*time.Second)\n\t\tdefer cancelFunc()\n\t\tif err := backend.TestConnection(testConnCtx); err != nil {\n\t\t\tl.Error(\"Failed to communicate with configured remote Loki backend, state history may not be persisted\", \"error\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn backend, nil\n\t}\n\n\tif backend == historian.BackendTypePrometheus {\n\t\tpcfg, err := historian.NewPrometheusConfig(cfg)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"invalid remote prometheus configuration: %w\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t\twriterCfg := writer.DatasourceWriterConfig{\n\t\t\tTimeout: cfg.PrometheusWriteTimeout,\n\t\t}\n\t\tlogCtx := log.WithContextualAttributes(ctx, []any{\"backend\", \"prometheus\"})\n\t\tprometheusBackendLogger := log.New(\"ngalert.state.historian\").FromContext(logCtx)\n\t\tw := writer.NewDatasourceWriter(writerCfg, datasourceService, httpClientProvider, pluginContextProvider, clock, prometheusBackendLogger, mw)\n\t\tif w == nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to create alert state metrics writer\")\n\t\t}\n\t\tbackend := historian.NewRemotePrometheusBackend(pcfg, w, prometheusBackendLogger, met)\n\n\t\treturn backend, nil\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"unrecognized state history backend: %s\", backend)\n}\n\nfunc configureNotificationHistorian(\n\tctx context.Context,\n\tfeatureToggles featuremgmt.FeatureToggles,\n\tcfg setting.UnifiedAlertingNotificationHistorySettings,\n\tmet *metrics.NotificationHistorian,\n\tl log.Logger,\n\ttracer tracing.Tracer,\n) (nfstatus.NotificationHistorian, error) {\n\tif !featureToggles.IsEnabled(ctx, featuremgmt.FlagAlertingNotificationHistory) || !cfg.Enabled {\n\t\tmet.Info.Set(0)\n\t\treturn nil, nil\n\t}\n\n\tmet.Info.Set(1)\n\tlcfg, err := lokiconfig.NewLokiConfig(cfg.LokiSettings)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"invalid remote loki configuration: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\treq := lokiclient.NewRequester()\n\tlogger := log.New(\"ngalert.notifier.historian\").FromContext(ctx)\n\tnh := notificationHistorian.NewNotificationHistorian(logger, lcfg, req, met.BytesWritten, met.WriteDuration, met.WritesTotal, five major components:\\n\\n## 1. Alert Rule Storage (pkg/services/ngalert/store/)\\nThe DBstore (database.go) is the central data persistence layer that implements the AlertingStore interface. It manages:\\n- Alert rules via alert_rule.go (GetAlertRulesForScheduling, DeleteAlertRulesByUID, etc.)\\n- Alert instances through InstanceDBStore (instance_database.go) for traditional storage and ProtoInstanceDBStore (proto_instance_database.go) for compressed protobuf storage\\n- Alertmanager configuration (alertmanager.go)\\n- Admin configuration (admin_configuration.go)\\n- Organization-level settings (org.go)\\n\\n## 2. Scheduler (pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/)\\nThe schedule package implements a rule evaluation engine:\\n- schedule.go: The main ScheduleService implements periodic evaluation loops, managing a registry of alert rules\\n- alert_rule.go: Evaluates individual alert rules based on query results\\n- recording_rule.go: Handles Prometheus-style recording rules\\n- registry.go: Maintains active rules and their evaluation state\\n- retry.go: Implements exponential backoff retry logic for failed evaluations\\n- ticker/ticker.go: Provides deterministic tick distribution for rule evaluation\\nThe scheduler pulls rules from the Store via RulesStore interface and sends evaluated alerts through AlertsSender to the notifier.\\n\\n## 3. State Manager (pkg/services/ngalert/state/)\\nThe Manager (manager.go) tracks alert state transitions and persistence:\\n- state.go: Defines State and StateTransitions structures representing alert status changes\\n- cache.go: In-memory cache of current alert states per organization\\n- persist.go: Defines InstanceStore interface for reading/writing alert instances\\n- persister_sync.go/persister_async.go/persister_sync_rule.go: Different persistence strategies (synchronous, asynchronous, or rule-based)\\n- multi_instance_reader.go: Reads state from multiple backends during startup for high-availability support\\n\\nThe state historian writes state history to multiple backends:\\n- historian/core.go: Historian interface and coordination\\n- historian/backend.go: Backend abstraction supporting multiple storage types\\n- historian/annotation.go: Stores history as Grafana annotations\\n- historian/loki.go: Remote Loki integration for state history\\n- historian/prometheus.go: Remote Prometheus integration via DatasourceWriter\\n- historian/multiple.go: Fan-out to multiple backends simultaneously\\n\\n## 4. Notifier (pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/)\\nThe MultiOrgAlertmanager (multiorg_alertmanager.go) manages per-organization Alertmanager instances:\\n- alertmanager.go: Wraps Prometheus Alertmanager for each organization (GrafanaAlertmanager)\\n- alertmanager_config.go: Manages Alertmanager configuration including routing rules and templates\\n- receiver_svc.go: Service for managing contact points/receivers\\n- silence_svc.go: Service for managing silences\\n- silences.go: Silence state management\\n- alerts.go: Formats and handles alert submission to Alertmanager\\n- config.go: Configuration parsing and validation\\n- crypto.go: Encryption of sensitive receiver configuration\\n- templates.go: Notification templates\\nThe MultiOrgAlertmanager uses Redis for HA clustering (redis_peer.go, redis_channel.go) and legacy storage for backward compatibility.\\n\\n## 5. Sender & History Writer (pkg/services/ngalert/sender/ and pkg/services/ngalert/writer/)\\nThe AlertsRouter (sender/router.go) is the central dispatcher:\\n- Routes evaluated alerts from the scheduler to either the internal MultiOrgAlertmanager or external Alertmanagers\\n- Syncs admin configuration periodically to determine alert routing\\n- Supports disabled organizations and multiple alertmanager backends\\n\\nThe DatasourceWriter (writer/datasourcewriter.go) writes metrics to remote storage:\\n- Supports writing to Prometheus-compatible remote write endpoints\\n- Used by the state historian for persistence in Prometheus\\n- Handles datasource selection and authentication\\n\\n## Interaction Flow\\n1. AlertNG.ProvideService initializes all components\\n2. AlertNG.Run starts the scheduler, state manager, alertmanager, and router concurrently\\n3. Scheduler evaluates rules fetched from Store\\n4. State Manager tracks state changes and persists via Historian\\n5. Historian writes to backends (Loki, Prometheus via DatasourceWriter, or Annotations)\\n6. AlertsRouter receives evaluated alerts and sends to MultiOrgAlertmanager\\n7. MultiOrgAlertmanager routes notifications to contact points based on configuration\\n\\nKey integration points:\\n- DBstore coordinates all data persistence\\n- State Manager bridges scheduler output and notifier input\\n- Historian enables state traceability across multiple backends\\n- AlertsRouter provides flexible notification routing\\n- Writer enables remote persistence of metrics and state\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":13,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3692,"cache_read_input_tokens":57119,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3692},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a86dff1d-5b5f-4174-8e54-b89b32685bbe","uuid":"8d4019f8-c945-482c-9135-2f9b3d4662c0"}

Notifier (pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/)\\nThe MultiOrgAlertmanager (multiorg_alertmanager.go) manages per-organization Alertmanager instances:\\n- alertmanager.go: Wraps Prometheus Alertmanager for each organization (GrafanaAlertmanager)\\n- alertmanager_config.go: Manages Alertmanager configuration including routing rules and templates\\n- receiver_svc.go: Service for managing contact points/receivers\\n- silence_svc.go: Service for managing silences\\n- silences.go: Silence state management\\n- alerts.go: Formats and handles alert submission to Alertmanager\\n- config.go: Configuration parsing and validation\\n- crypto.go: Encryption of sensitive receiver configuration\\n- templates.go: Notification templates\\nThe MultiOrgAlertmanager uses Redis for HA clustering (redis_peer.go, redis_channel.go) and legacy storage for backward compatibility.\\n\\n## 5. Sender & History Writer (pkg/services/ngalert/sender/ and pkg/services/ngalert/writer/)\\nThe AlertsRouter (sender/router.go) is the central dispatcher:\\n- Routes evaluated alerts from the scheduler to either the internal MultiOrgAlertmanager or external Alertmanagers\\n- Syncs admin configuration periodically to determine alert routing\\n- Supports disabled organizations and multiple alertmanager backends\\n\\nThe DatasourceWriter (writer/datasourcewriter.go) writes metrics to remote storage:\\n- Supports writing to Prometheus-compatible remote write endpoints\\n- Used by the state historian for persistence in Prometheus\\n- Handles datasource selection and authentication\\n\\n## Interaction Flow\\n1. AlertNG.ProvideService initializes all components\\n2. AlertNG.Run starts the scheduler, state manager, alertmanager, and router concurrently\\n3. Scheduler evaluates rules fetched from Store\\n4. State Manager tracks state changes and persists via Historian\\n5. Historian writes to backends (Loki, Prometheus via DatasourceWriter, or Annotations)\\n6. AlertsRouter receives evaluated alerts and sends to MultiOrgAlertmanager\\n7. MultiOrgAlertmanager routes notifications to contact points based on configuration\\n\\nKey integration points:\\n- DBstore coordinates all data persistence\\n- State Manager bridges scheduler output and notifier input\\n- Historian enables state traceability across multiple backends\\n- AlertsRouter provides flexible notification routing\\n- Writer enables remote persistence of metrics and state\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
